\begin{flushleft}
{\footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} This table shows daily retrun statistics for different cryptocurrencies. Descriptive statistics are expressed as percentages. The sample period spans from 2020-10-18 to 2026-02-03. The ADF test (Dickey \& Fuller, 1979, 1981) is used to examine stationarity; a statistically significant test statistic indicates rejection of the null hypothesis of a unit root, implying that the series is stationary. The Jarque--Bera test is used to assess normality; a statistically significant result indicates rejection of the null hypothesis of normality, suggesting that the distribution exhibits non-normal skewness and/or kurtosis. ***, **, * indicate significance at the 1\%, 5\%, and 10\% levels.}
\end{flushleft}

\begin{flushleft}
{\footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} The sample period spans from 2020-10-18 to 2026-02-03. Standard errors are reported in parentheses. $\log L$ denotes the maximized log-likelihood value. $\rho(\hat{\alpha}_{it},\tilde{\alpha}_{it})$ and $\rho(\Delta\hat{\alpha}_{it},\Delta\tilde{\alpha}_{it})$ are Pearson correlation coefficients between the estimated risk measures and their benchmarks. The key hyperparameter of the uPOT model is the threshold, which is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we also estimate the uPOT model using the 85\% and 90\% quantiles as alternative thresholds. The results indicate that the estimates are robust to the choice of the threshold, and the corresponding tables are available from the authors upon request. $^{***}$, $^{**}$, and $^{*}$ indicate significance at the 1\%, 5\%, and 10\% levels, respectively.
}
\end{flushleft}

\begin{flushleft}
{\footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} The sample period spans from 2020-10-18 to 2026-02-03. Standard errors are reported in parentheses. $\log L$ denotes the maximized log-likelihood value. $\rho(\hat{\alpha}_{it},\tilde{\alpha}_{it})$ and $\rho(\Delta\hat{\alpha}_{it},\Delta\tilde{\alpha}_{it})$ are Pearson correlation coefficients between the estimated risk measures and their benchmarks. The key hyperparameter of the uPOT model is the threshold, which is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we also estimate the uPOT model using the 85\% and 90\% quantiles as alternative thresholds. The results indicate that the estimates are robust to the choice of the threshold, and the corresponding tables are available from the authors upon request. $^{***}$, $^{**}$, and $^{*}$ indicate significance at the 1\%, 5\%, and 10\% levels, respectively.
}
\end{flushleft}

\end{adjustbox}
\begin{flushleft}
    \raggedright
    \footnotesize
    \textit{Notes:} This table reports lower-tail risk spillovers across currency markets. The sample period spans from 2020-10-18 to 2026-02-03. The $(i,j)$-th entry represents the estimated contribution of innovations in market $j$ to the forecast error variance of market $i$. The off-diagonal column sums (labeled \emph{Directional TO others}) and row sums (labeled \emph{Directional FROM others}) measure directional spillovers transmitted to and received from other markets, respectively, while the difference between the two (\emph{TO minus FROM}) captures net risk spillovers. The total risk spillover index, reported in the lower-right corner of the table, is defined as the ratio of the sum of all off-diagonal elements to the total sum of all elements (including diagonals), expressed as a percentage. The spillover table thus provides an approximate input--output decomposition of the total spillover index. Risk spillovers are estimated using a generalized vector autoregressive (VAR) framework following Diebold and Yilmaz (2012), based on forecast error variance decompositions of the reciprocal lower-tail index.
    \end{flushleft}
\end{table}

Net spillover & $1.87$ & $27.95$ & $1.42$ & $3.19$ & $0.77$ & $4.29$ & $-10.13$ & $21.08$ & $9.04$ & $7.24$ & $8.09$ & $-15.95$ & $0.61$ & $-17.27$ & $-12.71$ & $11.40$ & $10.51$ & $33.16$ & $24.31$ & $-13.93$ & $11.49$ & $16.22$ & $-9.81$ & $-2.80$ & $-12.05$ & $-11.28$ & $-3.98$ & $4.52$ & $-12.32$ & $-25.65$ & $-2.33$ & $7.38$ & $6.09$ & $-3.09$ & $19.56$ & $-20.46$ & $-5.58$ & $-12.47$ & $-6.16$ & $-1.40$ & $-12.99$ & $-7.78$ & $-17.14$ & $2.24$ & $24.88$ & $1.48$ & $-19.00$ & $8.07$ & $4.55$ & $-15.12$ & \hfill\shortstack[r]{Total spillover index\\ (4104.3/5000): 82.1\%} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{adjustbox}
\begin{flushleft}
    \raggedright
    \footnotesize
    \textit{Notes:} This table reports lower-tail risk spillovers across currency markets. The sample period spans from 2020-10-18 to 2026-02-03. The $(i,j)$-th entry represents the estimated contribution of innovations in market $j$ to the forecast error variance of market $i$. The off-diagonal column sums (labeled \emph{Directional TO others}) and row sums (labeled \emph{Directional FROM others}) measure directional spillovers transmitted to and received from other markets, respectively, while the difference between the two (\emph{TO minus FROM}) captures net risk spillovers. The total risk spillover index, reported in the lower-right corner of the table, is defined as the ratio of the sum of all off-diagonal elements to the total sum of all elements (including diagonals), expressed as a percentage. The spillover table thus provides an approximate input--output decomposition of the total spillover index. Risk spillovers are estimated using a generalized vector autoregressive (VAR) framework following Diebold and Yilmaz (2012), based on forecast error variance decompositions of the reciprocal lower-tail index.
    \end{flushleft}
\end{table}
\end{landscape}

% Notes for Lower-tail P_xi_exc
\vspace{1em}
{\centering
Figure X: Lower-Tail Risk Index and Negative Return Exceedances across Cryptocurrencies\\
}
\vspace{0.5em}
{\raggedright \footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} The red solid line represents the lower-tail index. This tail index is determined by the estimated parameters reported in Table X. The black vertical bars denote negative return exceedances beyond a predefined hurdle, which is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we also construct lower-tail indices using the 85\% and 90\% quantiles as alternative hurdles. The results indicate that the lower-tail index is robust to the choice of the threshold, and the corresponding figures are available from the authors upon request. Gray shaded bands highlight periods during which the tail index declines sharply. According to the peaks-over-threshold framework, a sharp decline in the tail index signals a rapid intensification of tail risk. Notably, these shaded intervals closely align with major cryptocurrency events.
}
\vspace{4em}

% Notes for Lower-tail P_std_sigma
\vspace{1em}
{\centering
Figure X: Standardized Dynamic Volatility of Negative Returns across Cryptocurrencies\\
}
\vspace{0.5em}
{\raggedright \footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} The red solid line depicts the standardized dynamic conditional volatility estimated using the GARCH(1,1) model, while the blue line shows the standardized dynamic conditional volatility obtained from the univariate peaks-over-threshold (uPOT) model, with parameters reported in Table X. The key hyperparameter of the uPOT model is the threshold, which is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we also construct standardized volatilities using the 85\% and 90\% quantiles as alternative thresholds. The results indicate that the standardized volatility estimates are robust to the choice of the threshold, and the corresponding figures are available from the authors upon request. A closer alignment between the two volatility series indicates greater reliability of the uPOT model estimation.
}
\vspace{4em}

% Notes for Upper-tail P_xi_exc
\vspace{1em}
{\centering
Figure X: Upper-Tail Risk Index and Positive Return Exceedances across Cryptocurrencies\\
}
\vspace{0.5em}
{\raggedright \footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} The red solid line represents the upper-tail index. This tail index is determined by the estimated parameters reported in Table X. The black vertical bars denote positive return exceedances beyond a predefined hurdle, which is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we also construct upper-tail indices using the 85\% and 90\% quantiles as alternative hurdles. The results indicate that the upper-tail index is robust to the choice of the threshold, and the corresponding figures are available from the authors upon request. Gray shaded bands highlight periods during which the tail index declines sharply. According to the peaks-over-threshold framework, a sharp decline in the tail index signals a rapid intensification of tail risk. Notably, these shaded intervals closely align with major cryptocurrency events.
}
\vspace{4em}

% Notes for Upper-tail P_std_sigma
\vspace{1em}
{\centering
Figure X: Standardized Dynamic Volatility of Positive Returns across Cryptocurrencies\\
}
\vspace{0.5em}
{\raggedright \footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} The red solid line depicts the standardized dynamic conditional volatility estimated using the GARCH(1,1) model, while the blue line shows the standardized dynamic conditional volatility obtained from the univariate peaks-over-threshold (uPOT) model, with parameters reported in Table X. The key hyperparameter of the uPOT model is the threshold, which is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we also construct standardized volatilities using the 85\% and 90\% quantiles as alternative thresholds. The results indicate that the standardized volatility estimates are robust to the choice of the threshold, and the corresponding figures are available from the authors upon request. A closer alignment between the two volatility series indicates greater reliability of the uPOT model estimation.
}
\vspace{4em}

% Notes for Lower-tail dynamic net spillovers
\vspace{1.5em}
{\centering
Figure X: Lower-Tail Dynamic Net Spillovers across Cryptocurrencies\\
}
\vspace{0.5em}
{\raggedright \footnotesize
\textit{Notes:} This figure illustrates the dynamic net risk spillovers from each coin to all other coins in the set. Net risk spillovers are computed as the difference between risk spillovers transmitted to other coins and risk spillovers received from them. Risk spillovers are estimated using a generalized vector autoregressive (VAR) framework following Diebold and Yilmaz (2012), based on forecast error variance decompositions of the reciprocal lower-tail index. The rolling-window size of the VAR model is set to 200 days, and the threshold of the univariate peaks-over-threshold (uPOT) model is set at the 95\% quantile. As part of robustness checks, we additionally construct net spillover measures using alternative thresholds at the 85\% and 90\% quantiles, as well as alternative window sizes of 150 and 250 days. The results indicate that the dynamic net spillover estimates are robust to the choice of both the window size and the threshold. The corresponding figures are available from the authors upon request.
}
\vspace{4em}

% Notes for Upper-tail dynamic net spillovers
\vspace{1.5em}
{\centering
Figure X: Upper-Tail Dynamic Net Spillovers across Cryptocurrencies\\
}
\vspace{0.5em}
{\raggedright \footnotesize

% Network plot
\begin{landscape}
\begin{figure}[htbp]
    \centering
    \includegraphics[width=0.48\linewidth]{./result/DY/percent95win200/network_plot_up.pdf}
    \hfill
    \includegraphics[width=0.48\linewidth]{./result/DY/percent95win200/network_plot_down.pdf}
    \caption{Upper-tail (left) and Lower-tail (right) network risk spillover, rolling-window size = 200 days, uPOT threshold = 0.95}
    \label{fig:network_up_down}

    \vspace{0.5em}
    \begin{minipage}{\linewidth}
    \footnotesize\raggedright
    \textit{Notes:} Blue nodes denote net risk spillover transmitters, while orange nodes denote net risk spillover receivers. The size of each node reflects the magnitude of its net risk spillover transmission or net risk absorption intensity. The thickness of each directed edge reflects the magnitude of risk spillovers, with arrows pointing from risk-exporting currencies to risk-importing currencies. Red edges indicate intensities exceeding 50\%.
    \end{minipage}
\end{figure}
\end{landscape}

    \end{subfigure}

    \caption{Lower-tail Network risk spillover under alternative rolling-window sizes and uPOT thresholds}
    \label{fig:lower_network_robwin_up_down}

    \vspace{0.5em}
    \begin{minipage}{\linewidth}
    \footnotesize\raggedright
    \textit{Notes:} Blue nodes denote net risk spillover transmitters, while orange nodes denote net risk spillover receivers. The size of each node reflects the magnitude of its net risk spillover transmission or net risk absorption intensity. The thickness of each directed edge reflects the magnitude of risk spillovers, with arrows pointing from risk-exporting currencies to risk-importing currencies. Gray edges indicate normalized spillover intensities between 50\% and 75\% of the global maximum, whereas red edges indicate intensities exceeding 75\%. These thresholds are chosen to reduce visual clutter and highlight economically meaningful spillover channels.
    \end{minipage}
\end{figure}

        \centering
        \includegraphics[width=\linewidth]{./result/Robustness/rank45plot/win150up.pdf}
        \caption{}
    \end{subfigure}

        \centering
        \includegraphics[width=\linewidth]{./result/Robustness/rank45plot/win250up.pdf}
        \caption{}
    \end{subfigure}

    \caption{Rankings of the upper-tail net risk spillover effect for each currency based on different rolling-window sizes and uPOT thresholds}
    \label{fig:upper_rank45}

    \vspace{0.5em}
    \begin{minipage}{\linewidth}
    \footnotesize\raggedright
    \textit{Notes:} The vertical axis represents the ranking of net risk spillovers based on the benchmark hyperparameter (i.e. rolling-window = 200 days, uPOT threshold = 0.95), while the horizontal axis shows the ranking based on alternative hyperparameters. The $45^\circ$ line serves as a benchmark for assessing the consistency of rankings between alternative and the benchmark hyperparameters. If a point falls on the $45^\circ$ line, it indicates that the relative rankings of net risk spillovers for currencies are identical across different hyperparameter settings.
    \end{minipage}
\end{figure}
